Question #1 (ID: 486001)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Gentility} & \text{behaves} & \text{anyone whimsically.} \\ \text{And he who} & \text{possesses} & \text{the symbol of peace and humanity.} \\ \text{A gentle man} & \text{is} & \text{this quality is a gentleman.} \\ \text{He} & \text{never hurts} & \text{the state of being gentle.} \\ \text{} & \text{} & \text{with all gently.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Gentility is the state of being gentle.b. And he who possesses this quality is a gentleman.c. A gentle man behaves with all gently.d. He never hurts anyone whimsically.e. He is the symbol of peace and humanity.

Explanation:
Choose one phrase from each column to form a subject + verb + object/complement so the sentence is grammatically complete and meaningful. For example, "A gentle man is the symbol of peace and humanity" correctly combines the subject "A gentle man", the verb "is", and the complement "the symbol of peace and humanity", producing a clear, correct sentence.

Question #2 (ID: 486002)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Time and tide} & \text{} & \text{lost forever.} \\ \text{No one} & \text{is} & \text{call it back.} \\ \text{Money} & \text{wait} & \text{for none.} \\ \text{Health also} & \text{can} & \text{be regained.} \\ \text{But time once lost} & \text{} & \text{be regained.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Time and tide wait for none.b. No one can call it back.c. Money can be regained.d. Health also can be regained.e. But time once lost is lost forever.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: প্রতিটি বাক্য টেবিলের প্রথম কলাম থেকে বিষয়, দ্বিতীয় কলাম থেকে ক্রিয়া ও তৃতীয় কলাম থেকে বাকির অংশ বেছে নিয়ে তৈরি করা হয়েছে, ফলে শব্দগুলো যোগ করলে ব্যাকরণগতভাবে সঠিক ও অর্থপূর্ণ বাক্য হয়। উদাহরণ হিসেবে "Time and tide" + "wait" + "for none." → "Time and tide wait for none."—এইভাবে টেবিলের অংশগুলো বিনিময় করে মোট পাঁচটি অর্থপূর্ণ বাক্য সংগ্রহ করা যায়।

Question #3 (ID: 486003)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Newspapers} & \text{gives} & \text{us news of home and abroad.} \\ \text{It} & \text{has} & \text{useful to all section of people.} \\ \text{They} & \text{are} & \text{great educative value too.} \\ \text{} & \text{present} & \text{really a part and parcel of our life.} \\ \text{} & \text{} & \text{us the outside world like a mirror.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Newspapers are useful to all sections of people.b. It gives us news of home and abroad.c. It has great educative value too.d. They present us the outside world like a mirror.e. They are really part and parcel of our life.

Explanation:
Use the table by choosing a subject from column 1 + a verb from column 2 + a complement from column 3, and make small grammar adjustments (subject–verb agreement, articles, word order). For example: Newspapers give us news of home and abroad; It is useful to all sections of people; They are of great educative value too; Newspapers have really become a part and parcel of our life; They show us the outside world like a mirror.

Question #4 (ID: 486004)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Traffic jam} & \text{are} & \text{offices in time.} \\ \text{It} & \text{cannot reach} & \text{the worst sufferers of traffic jam.} \\ \text{The service holders} & \text{must be taken} & \text{a common feature of city life today} \\ \text{The patients} & \text{causes} & \text{to minimize traffic jam} \\ \text{Effective measures} & \text{is} & \text{many problems for the urban people} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Traffic jam is a common feature of city life today.b. It causes many problems for the urban people.c. The service holders cannot reach offices in time.d. The patients are the worst sufferers of traffic jam.e. Effective measures must be taken to minimize traffic jam.

Explanation:
Explanation:
1. Traffic jam is a common feature of city life today.
2. It causes many problems for the urban people.
3. The service holders are the worst sufferers of traffic jam.
4. The patients cannot reach offices in time.
5. Effective measures must be taken to minimize traffic jam.

These sentences are made by choosing a subject from column 1, an appropriate verb from column 2, and a matching phrase from column 3, while ensuring correct grammar and logical meaning (for example, using "is" with "traffic jam" and matching singular/plural forms). This substitution method teaches how to combine sentence parts correctly to form meaningful, grammatically correct sentences.

Question #5 (ID: 486005)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Computer} & \text{is/are} & \text{used for using power point.} \\ \text{Mobile phone} & \text{isn't/aren't} & \text{used for speaking with others.} \\ \text{Modern technology} & \text{have to} & \text{always safe for us.} \\ \text{We} & \text{} & \text{used for composing a document.} \\ \text{} & \text{} & \text{ensure the safe use of modern technology.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Computer is used for using PowerPoint.b. Computer is also used for composing a document.c. Mobile phone is used for speaking with others.d. Modern technology isn't always safe for us.e. We have to ensure the safe use of modern technology.

Explanation:
Use singular verbs with singular nouns: "Computer" and "Mobile phone" take "is"/"isn't" (not "are"/"aren't"), and use the passive "is/are used for" when the device receives the action (e.g., "A computer is used for making PowerPoint presentations").  
Use active voice when the subject does the action ("We use a computer to compose a document"), and change "have to" to "has to" with the singular noun "Modern technology" and add "be" for correct obligation ("Modern technology has to be always safe for us").  
The final line is an imperative command — "Ensure the safe use of modern technology" — which correctly asks someone to take action; keep simple present tense for general facts and habitual uses.

Question #6 (ID: 486006)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Socrates} & \text{was} & \text{accused of disloyalty.} \\ \text{The young men} & \text{grew} & \text{to spread knowledge among the people.} \\ \text{The rulers of Athens} & \text{began} & \text{jealous of his popularity.} \\ \text{He} & \text{was} & \text{sentenced to gather round him.} \\ \text{They} & \text{sentenced} & \text{him to death.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Socrates began to spread knowledge among the people.b. The young men began to gather round him.c. The rulers of Athens grew jealous of his popularity.d. He was accused of disloyalty.e. They sentenced him to death.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: এখানে প্রতিটি সারি থেকে একটি পূর্ণ বাক্য তৈরি করা হয় — প্রথম অংশ সাবজেক্ট, দ্বিতীয় অংশ ক্রিয়া, তৃতীয় অংশ অবজেক্ট/কমপ্লিমেন্ট হিসেবে কাজ করে। বাক্য গঠনে ক্রিয়ার ধরন লক্ষ করে সঠিক সম্পূরক ব্যবহার করতে হয় (যেমন "began" হলে সাধারণত "to" সহ বা "became" ব্যবহার করা ভালো), ফলে প্রতিটি সারি থেকে সহজেই মানসম্পন্ন পাঁচটি বাক্য পাওয়া যায়।

Question #7 (ID: 486007)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Man} & \text{wants} & \text{curious by nature} \\ \text{He} & \text{has} & \text{a great educative value} \\ \text{Newspaper} & \text{is} & \text{to know various things of the world} \\ \text{It} & \text{shows} & \text{the best way to satisfy his curiosity} \\ \text{} & \text{} & \text{us the outside world like a mirror} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Man is curious by nature.b. He wants to know various things of the world.c. Newspaper is the best way to satisfy his curiosity.d. It shows us the outside world like a mirror.e. It has a great educative value.

Explanation:
Pick one item from each column in order (subject + verb + complement) and adjust small words (a/an, auxiliary verbs, pronouns) so the result is grammatically natural. For example, choosing "Man" + "is" + "curious by nature" gives "A man is curious by nature"; do the same with other column combinations to make five correct sentences.

Question #8 (ID: 486008)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{An educated mother} & \text{plays} & \text{indebted to its educated mothers.} \\ \text{A child} & \text{is} & \text{the key role in building up an educated nation.} \\ \text{If the mother} & \text{should} & \text{be educated.} \\ \text{An educated nation} & \text{be} & \text{always in touch with its mother.} \\ \text{So, all mothers} & \text{} & \text{educated, her children will be educated.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. An educated mother plays the key role in building up an educated nation.b. A child is always in touch with its mother.c. If the mother is educated, her children will be educated.d. An educated nation should be indebted to its educated mothers.e. So, all mothers should be educated.

Explanation:
Explanation: Form each sentence by picking one phrase from the first column (subject), one from the second (verb or auxiliary), and one from the third (object/complement) so you produce a complete subject–verb–complement structure. Ensure grammatical agreement and logical sense (for example, "An educated mother" + "plays" + "the key role in building up an educated nation" or "If the mother" + "should" + "be educated, her children will be educated"), and adjust punctuation or helpers (like adding "if" or "are") when needed. This way you can make five correct sentences by combining different items while keeping meaning and grammar correct.

Question #9 (ID: 486009)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Sincerity} & \text{are} & \text{indifferent to the importance of sincerity.} \\ \text{A sincere man} & \text{is} & \text{properly.} \\ \text{The great people} & \text{works} & \text{not aware of its importance.} \\ \text{The people of our country} & \text{} & \text{also sincere to their work.} \\ \text{They} & \text{are} & \text{a great virtue.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Sincerity is a great virtue.b. A sincere man works properly.c. The great people are also sincere to their work.d. The people of our country are not aware of its importance.e. They are indifferent to the importance of sincerity.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: প্রতিটি বাক্য তৈরির জন্য টেবিলের প্রথম কলাম থেকে বিষয়, দ্বিতীয় কলাম থেকে ক্রিয়া ও তৃতীয় কলাম থেকে বাক্যাংশ নিলে পূর্ণ বাক্য হয়; কিন্তু বিষয় ও ক্রিয়ার মধ্যে সংখ্যা ও রূপের মিল (subject–verb agreement) রাখাটা জরুরি। উদাহরণস্বরূপ, "A sincere man is properly." এ ক্ষেত্রে "A sincere man" একবচন হওয়ায় "is" ঠিক এবং "They are a great virtue." এ ক্ষেত্রে "They" বহুবচন হওয়ায় "are" ব্যবহার সঠিক। এই নিয়ম মেনে টেবিল থেকে উপযুক্ত তিনটি অংশ যেকোনোভাবে মিলিয়ে অর্থবহ পাঁচটি বাক্য বানানো যায়।

Question #10 (ID: 486010)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Every nation} & \text{has} & \text{every year with due solemnity.} \\ \text{Our nation} & \text{are} & \text{some glorious days.} \\ \text{These days} & \text{is} & \text{21st February, 25th March, 16th December, etc.} \\ \text{The 16th December} & \text{must have} & \text{a glorious day for the people of Bangladesh.} \\ \text{} & \text{is observed} & \text{also some glorious and memorable days.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Every nation must have some glorious days.b. Our nation has also some glorious and memorable days.c. These days are 21st February, 26th March, 16th December, etc.d. The 16th December is a glorious day for the people of Bangladesh.e. The 16th December is observed every year with due solemnity.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: টেবিলটির প্রথম কলাম সাবজেক্ট, দ্বিতীয় কলাম ক্রিয়া এবং তৃতীয় কলাম বাক্যের বাকি অংশ প্রদর্শন করে; একটি ঠিকঠাক বাক্য গঠনের জন্য S–V–O ক্রমানুসারে একেকটি টুকরা বেছে নেয়া হয়। সাবজেক্ট ও ক্রিয়ার মধ্যে সংখ্যা ও রূপ মিলতে হবে (যেমন "These days" বহুবচন — তাই "are" হবে), এবং বাক্যের অর্থ পাওয়ার জন্য ক্রিয়া ও অব্যয়াংশের সাথে মিলিয়ে যুক্তাংশগুলো coherently সাজাতে হবে (যেমন তারিখগুলো বিবৃতির অংশ হিসেবে ব্যবহার করা হয়, "16th December"‑এর ক্ষেত্রে "must have a glorious day" বা "is observed" প্রভৃতি)। এই নিয়ম অনুসরণ করলেই টেবিল থেকে পাঁচটি স্বাভাবিক ও ব্যাকরণগতভাবে সঠিক বাক্য তৈরি করা যাবে।

Question #11 (ID: 486011)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Sincerity} & \text{should be} & \text{in the long run.} \\ \text{A sincere person} & \text{be} & \text{the root of all success.} \\ \text{He} & \text{suffer} & \text{able to go a long way.} \\ \text{Insincere people} & \text{becomes} & \text{sincere in every affair of our daily life.} \\ \text{So, we} & \text{} & \text{Successful in life.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Sincerity is the root of all success.b. A sincere person is able to go a long way.c. He becomes successful in life.d. Insincere people suffer in the long run.e. So, we should be sincere in every affair of our daily life.

Explanation:
প্রতিটি বাক্য গঠনের নিয়ম হলো: টেবিলের প্রথম কলামের বিষয়, দ্বিতীয় কলামের ক্রিয়া ও তৃতীয় কলামের বাক্যাংশ এক করে লিখতে হবে এবং বাক্যকে স্বভাবসিদ্ধ করতে প্রয়োজনমত ক্রিয়ার সঠিক রূপ (is/are/is able ইত্যাদি) ব্যবহার করতে হবে। এজন্য কয়েকটি সংশোধন করতে হয়—উদাহরণ: "A sincere person be the root of all success." → "A sincere person is the root of all success." এবং "He suffer able to go a long way." → "He is able to go a long way." এইভাবে বিষয়‑ক্রিয়া সামঞ্জস্য বজায় রেখে পাঁচটি শুদ্ধ বাক্য তৈরি করা যায়।

Question #12 (ID: 486012)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Poverty} & \text{has} & \text{much probability of development.} \\ \text{It} & \text{is} & \text{too complicated to solve in a day.} \\ \text{Our country} & \text{makes} & \text{us disreputable in the society.} \\ \text{We} & \text{should solve} & \text{this problem through hard diligence.} \\ \text{} & \text{} & \text{been actually created by us.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Poverty is too complicated to solve in a day.b. It has been actually created by us.c. It makes us disreputable in the society.d. Our country has much probability of development.e. We should solve this problem through hard diligence.

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: প্রতিটি সারি থেকে প্রথম কলামের শব্দকে বিষয় (subject), দ্বিতীয় কলামের শব্দকে ক্রিয়া (verb) এবং তৃতীয় কলামের বাক্যাংশকে অবশিষ্ট অংশ হিসেবে নিয়ে Subject + Verb + Object/Complement ক্রমে মিলিয়ে পূর্ণ বাক্য বানাতে হয়। বাক্য গঠনের সময় ব্যক্তি ও সংখ্যার সম্মতি চেক করতে হবে এবং যেখানে প্রয়োজন passive বা auxiliary যোগ করতে হবে — যেমন পঞ্চম সারি বিষয়/ক্রিয়া নেই, তাই "It has been actually created by us." বা "This has been actually created by us." এর মতো রূপ ব্যবহার করে পূর্ণ বাক্য করা যায়।

Question #13 (ID: 486013)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{Independence} & \text{went} & \text{the war.} \\ \text{No nation} & \text{took place} & \text{to the battlefield to liberate the country.} \\ \text{Our war of independence} & \text{be} & \text{it without struggle.} \\ \text{People of all walks of life} & \text{can achieve} & \text{in 1971.} \\ \text{They} & \text{joined} & \text{the birth right of a nation.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Independence is the birth right of a nation.b. No nation can achieve it without struggle.c. Our war of independence took place in 1971.d. People of all walks of life joined the war.e. They went to the battlefield to liberate the country.

Explanation:
Our war of independence took place in 1971.
People of all walks of life went to the battlefield to liberate the country.
No nation can achieve independence without struggle.
They joined the war.
Independence is the birth right of a nation.

Explanation:
Each sentence is made by choosing a suitable subject (column 1), verb (column 2) and object/complement (column 3) and adjusting verb forms for correct grammar. If a given phrase is unclear (like "it without struggle"), replace the pronoun with the appropriate noun ("independence") so the sentence is meaningful.

Question #14 (ID: 486014)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Make five sentences from the following substitution table.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|} \hline \text{A teacher} & \text{can hold} & \text{an architect of a nation.} \\ \text{He} & \text{is} & \text{an important role in building up an educated nation.} \\ \text{A good teacher} & \text{plays} & \text{to remove the darkness of ignorance from the society.} \\ \text{His vision} & \text{removes} & \text{the attention of his students in the class.} \\ \text{In fact, he} & \text{} & \text{a philosopher and a guide to his students.} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. A teacher is an architect of a nation.b. He plays an important role in building up an educated nation.c. A good teacher can hold the attention of his students in the class.d. His vision is to remove the darkness of ignorance from the society.e. In fact, he is a philosopher and a guide to his students.

Explanation:
Each sentence is formed by choosing the subject (first column), the verb or verb phrase (second column) and the complement (third column) and then making small grammatical adjustments so the result is natural and meaningful (for example, use a linking verb like "is" or add "be called" when needed). Ensure subject-verb agreement and that the verb correctly links to the complement (e.g., "He plays an important role..." not "He is an important role"). Keep the meaning clear by correcting awkward phrasing or missing words while preserving the original ideas from the table.

Row five has no verb in the middle column, so the simple verb "die" is used to complete that sentence.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. Happiness is a relative term.b. A person with a crown may not be happy.c. Whereas a day labourer may find happiness living in a shabby hut.d. Again, happiness varies from person to person.e. Complete happiness or peace of mind is a blessing of God.

Explanation:

 late to go for office. A huge amount of fuel [math]\textbf{is\ wasted}[/math]
 in the roads. But there are some valid reasons for traffic jam. Drivers tend to [math]\textbf{overtake}[/math]
 each other frequently. Most of the drivers are unable to read and write. So they [math]\textbf{do\ not}[/math]
 understand the meanings of different symbols in the roads while driving.a. Singular subject “it” → present simple with “s” → "causes". b. Plural subject “we” → base verb → "get". c. Passive present → “is wasted”. d. After “to” → base verb → "overtake". e. Negative sentence with plural subject → "do not understand".

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|l|l|} \hline \textbf{sacrifice} & \textbf{work} & \textbf{follow} & \textbf{know} & \textbf{have} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Love for one’s country is (a) — as patriotism. Every man (b) — great love for his country. Many of our freedom fighters (c) — their lives in 1971 for the sake of our country due to their noble virtue. At present, still there are some people who (d) — relentlessly for the sake of our country because they love our country. We should (e) — their footprint.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. known b. has c. sacrificed d. work e. follow

Explanation:
Love for one’s country is \textbf{known} as patriotism. Every man \textbf{has} great love for his country. Many of our freedom fighters \textbf{sacrificed} their lives in 1971 for the sake of our country due to their noble virtue. At present, still there are some people who \textbf{work} relentlessly for the sake of our country because they love our country. We should \textbf{follow} their footprint.(a) General truth in passive → "is known". (b) Third person singular (man) requires present simple form of “have” → "has". (c) Past action in 1971 → simple past "sacrificed". (d) Ongoing/habitual action in present → use base form "work". (e) Modal verb "should" followed by base form → "follow".

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Complete the following text with suitable verbs in the box with their right forms.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|l|l|} \hline \textbf{vary} & \textbf{be} & \textbf{find} & \textbf{have} & \textbf{earn} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Happiness is a relative term. A person with a crown living in a place may not be happy whereas a day labourer may (a) — happiness living in a shabby hut. Again happiness (b) — from person to person. A beggar can be happy if he (c) — a coin but a businessman who can (d) — a huge sum of money a day may not be happy. Happiness (e) — only the blessing of Allah.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. find b. varies c. has d. earn e. is

Explanation:
Happiness is a relative term. A person with a crown living in a place may not be happy whereas a day labourer may \textbf{find} happiness living in a shabby hut. Again happiness \textbf{varies} from person to person. A beggar can be happy if he \textbf{has} a coin but a businessman who can \textbf{earn} a huge sum of money a day may not be happy. Happiness \textbf{is} only the blessing of Allah.(a) "May" is a modal, followed by base form → "find". (b) "Happiness" is singular → third person singular verb "varies". (c) Present conditional structure → "has". (d) After modal "can" → base form "earn". (e) General truth about happiness → use present simple "is".

Question:

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|l|} \hline \textbf{give} & \textbf{take} & \textbf{have} & \textbf{commit} & \textbf{afford} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Drugs (a) — a terrible effect on social life. It (b) — the addicts to an unreal world of dreams. This is called hallucination. And this hallucination (c) — rise to social crimes. When the drug addicts cannot (d) — to buy drugs, they (e) — many kinds of social crimes.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. have b. takes c. gives d. afford e. commit

Explanation:

And this hallucination \textbf{gives} rise to social crimes. (c) “Give rise to” is a fixed expression → use "gives". (d) After “cannot” → base verb “afford”. (e) “They” + crimes → verb = “commit” (collocational verb with "crime").

He gave the man some money and \textbf{set} him free.(a) “Did no wrong” is a common phrase → simple past. (b) Action in past → simple past "visited". (c) Reported speech → use past form "was". (d) Result of inquiry → past simple "found". (e) “Set free” is a fixed expression → simple past "set".

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|l|l|} \hline \textbf{adopt} & \textbf{rise} & \textbf{be} & \textbf{achieve} & \textbf{try} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Honesty is a great virtue. An honest man is liked and trusted by all. The ignorant men adopt unfair means with a view to (a) — their objectives. An honest man may (b) — poor, but he never (c) — to become rich by (d) — dishonest means. His rise in life may be slow, but he (e) — very high in the long run.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. achieving b. be c. tries d. adopting e. rises

Explanation:
Honesty is a great virtue. An honest man is liked and trusted by all. The ignorant men adopt unfair means with a view to \textbf{achieving} their objectives. An honest man may \textbf{be} poor, but he never \textbf{tries} to become rich by \textbf{adopting} dishonest means. His rise in life may be slow, but he \textbf{rises} very high in the long run.(a) “With a view to” → followed by gerund “achieving”. (b) After modal “may” → base form “be”. (c) Negative present simple → “tries”. (d) After “by” → use gerund “adopting”. (e) Present simple → “rises”.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Complete the following text with suitable verbs in the box with their right forms.

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|l|l|} \hline \textbf{come} & \textbf{make} & \textbf{tell} & \textbf{gain} & \textbf{trust} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Truthfulness is one of the greatest virtues which (a) — a man really great. A man is not (b) — by others if he does not cultivate the habit of speaking the truth. A man who is not trusted by anybody can (c) — any position. A man can achieve his ends once or twice by (d) — lies, but no permanent gain is possible. So, a man can achieve success if he (e) — truthful.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
a. makes b. trusted c. gain d. telling e. is

Explanation:
Truthfulness is one of the greatest virtues which \textbf{makes} a man really great. A man is not \textbf{trusted} by others if he does not cultivate the habit of speaking the truth. A man who is not trusted by anybody can \textbf{gain} any position. A man can achieve his ends once or twice by \textbf{telling} lies, but no permanent gain is possible. So, a man can achieve success if he \textbf{is} truthful.(a) “Which makes” → relative clause present. (b) Passive → “is trusted”. (c) After modal “can” → base form “gain”. (d) After preposition “by” → use gerund “telling”. (e) Conditional structure → “if he is”.

Question:

[math]\begin{array}{|l|l|l|l|l|} \hline \textbf{reduce} & \textbf{are} & \textbf{have} & \textbf{is} & \textbf{adopt} \\ \hline \end{array}[/math]

Options:

Explanation:

(e) "It is" is a fixed expression for emphasizing importance → "is". (f) Infinitive form after "to" → "adopt".

Question #87 (ID: 485910)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) He said to me, “What are you doing now?”

(b) She said, “Hurrah! We have passed the exam.”

(c) I said to him, “Don't go there.”

(d) The teacher said, “Water boils at 100°C.”

(e) They said, “We were watching TV last night.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) He asked me what I was doing then.

(b) She exclaimed with joy that they had passed the exam.

(c) I told him not to go there.

(d) The teacher said that water boils at 100°C.

(e) They said that they had been watching TV the previous night.

Explanation:
(a) WH-question → "what are you" becomes "what I was"; "now" → "then".

(b) Exclamatory with emotion → "Hurrah!" becomes "exclaimed with joy"; tense = past perfect.

(c) Imperative negative → "told not to"; verb becomes infinitive.

(d) General truth → no tense change, remains in present.

(e) Past continuous → becomes past perfect continuous; "last night" becomes "the previous night".

Question #88 (ID: 485911)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) I said, “Can you help me?”

(b) He said to her, “Don't waste your time.”

(c) She said, “I will come tomorrow.”

(d) The man said, “Alas! I am ruined.”

(e) He said to me, “What is your name?”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) I asked if he could help me.

(b) He advised her not to waste her time.

(c) She said that she would come the next day.

(d) The man exclaimed with sorrow that he was ruined.

(e) He asked me what my name was.

Explanation:
(a) Interrogative with modal → "Can you" becomes "if he could".

(b) Negative command → "advised not to", possessive pronoun changes.

(c) Future → "will" becomes "would"; "tomorrow" → "the next day".

(d) "Alas!" = sorrow → "exclaimed with sorrow".

(e) WH-question → "what is" becomes "what my name was".

Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(e) They said, “We had finished our work.”

Options:

(e) They said that they had finished their work.

Explanation:
(a) Universal truth → tense remains unchanged.

(b) Present continuous becomes past continuous.

(c) Interrogative with modal → "will" becomes "would", pronouns shift.

(d) "Please" → request → "requested", verb becomes infinitive.

(e) Past perfect remains unchanged in indirect speech.

(b) He said that he had been reading that book.

(c) They asked us if we knew the answer.

(d) The man ordered to bring him some water.

(e) The boy exclaimed with joy that he had got the prize.

Explanation:

(b) Present perfect continuous → past perfect continuous; "this" → "that".

(c) Interrogative → "Do you know" → "if we knew".

(d) Command → "ordered", verb becomes "to bring".

(e) Emotion → "Hurrah!" becomes "exclaimed with joy", tense becomes past perfect.

(b) Present continuous → remains same in indirect.

(c) Imperative → "told to", verb in infinitive form.

(d) Negative past → becomes past perfect.

(e) “Let us” → proposal → “proposed that we should”.

Question #93 (ID: 485916)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) He said to me, "You have done your work."

(b) Abir says, "I can help you."

(c) Arif said to me, "Do you want my help?"

(d) Mother said to me, "Do not run in the sun."

(e) They said to me, "Let us decide the matter ourselves."

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) He told me that I had done my work.

(b) Abir says that he can help me.

(c) Arif asked me if I wanted his help.

(d) Mother told me not to run in the sun.

(e) They proposed to me that we should decide the matter ourselves.

Explanation:
(a) The reporting verb "said to" is changed to "told", and present perfect "have done" becomes past perfect "had done" to match the reporting verb in past.

(b) Since the reporting verb "says" is in present tense, the tense inside the quotation remains unchanged; "I" becomes "he" and "you" becomes "me".

(c) It's a question, so we use "asked" and "Do you want" changes to "if I wanted"; pronouns are adjusted accordingly.

(d) This is a negative command. "Said to" becomes "told", and the imperative is transformed using "not to run".

(e) "Let us" expresses a proposal, so we use "proposed that we should"; "ourselves" remains contextual.

Question #94 (ID: 485917)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) I said to the man, “Do you know anybody here?”

(b) Maruf said, “Let us go for a picnic.”

(c) She said, “Let him do it again.”

(d) Father said to me, “Don’t tell a lie.”

(e) The teacher said to us, “Make good use of your time.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) I asked the man if he knew anybody there.

(b) Maruf proposed that we should go for a picnic.

(c) She suggested that he should do it again.

(d) Father advised me not to tell a lie.

(e) The teacher advised us to make good use of our time.

Explanation:
(a) "Said to" becomes "asked" as it’s a question, and "Do you know" changes to "if he knew"; "here" becomes "there".

(b) "Let us" implies a suggestion; so "proposed" is used followed by "that we should go".

(c) "Let him" suggests permission or suggestion; thus we use "suggested that he should".

(d) Negative command changes "said to" to "advised", and "Don’t tell" becomes "not to tell".

(e) An imperative statement; we convert "said to" into "advised", and the rest into infinitive form.

Question #95 (ID: 485918)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) She said, “I was reading a book last night.”

(b) He said, “By Allah, I will never disobey you.”

(c) Tina says to her sister, “Will you go to market?”

(d) He said to me, “Study attentively.”

(e) The teacher said, “The July Revolution of 2024 changed the image of Bangladesh to the world.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) She said that she had been reading a book the previous night.

(b) He swore by Allah that he would never disobey me.

(c) Tina asks her sister if she will go to market.

(d) He advised me to study attentively.

(e) The teacher said that the July Revolution of 2024 had changed the image of Bangladesh to the world.

Explanation:
(a) Past continuous tense "was reading" changes to past perfect continuous "had been reading"; "last night" becomes "the previous night".

(b) This is an oath. "Said" is replaced with "swore", and "will never disobey" becomes "would never disobey"; pronouns are changed.

(c) Reporting verb is in present, so the verb "will" remains unchanged; "says to" becomes "asks".

(d) Imperative sentence; "said to" is changed to "advised", and "Study attentively" becomes "to study attentively".

(e) This is a statement of past fact; so "changed" becomes "had changed" for reported speech consistency.

Question #96 (ID: 485919)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) "I am a student," the girl says.

(b) The man said, “Abu Sayeed was a student activist during July Revolution.”

(c) The teacher said, “Make sure to bring your raincoats today.”

(d) The girl said, “I have never eaten hilsa before.”

(e) The man said, “What a beautiful sunset!”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The girl says that she is a student.

(b) The man said that Abu Sayeed had been a student activist during the July Revolution.

(c) The teacher advised us to make sure to bring our raincoats that day.

(d) The girl said that she had never eaten hilsa before.

(e) The man exclaimed that it was a very beautiful sunset.

Explanation:
(a) "Says" is in present tense, so no change in verb tense; direct quote becomes indirect with "that".

(b) "Was" becomes "had been" to maintain backshift in past tense; no pronoun change needed.

(c) Imperative with "said" becomes "advised", and "today" becomes "that day"; possessive pronoun "your" becomes "our".

(d) Present perfect changes to past perfect "had never eaten"; no further changes as it's a statement.

(e) Exclamatory sentence is converted using "exclaimed that" and emotional phrase is restructured to positive statement "very beautiful sunset".

Question #97 (ID: 485920)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) The woman said to the passerby, "Excuse me, do you know the way to the railway station?"

(b) Liza said, "Good morning, Riaz."

(c) The man said, "The dengue fever outbreak in Dhaka last year was very concerning."

(d) She said, "I will come by 5 o’clock."

(e) The boy said, "Yay! We scored three goals."

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The woman politely asked the passerby if he knew the way to the railway station.

(b) Liza greeted Riaz good morning.

(c) The man said that the dengue fever outbreak in Dhaka the previous year had been very concerning.

(d) She said that she would come by 5 o’clock.

(e) The boy exclaimed with joy that they had scored three goals.

Explanation:
(a) This is a polite question. "Said to" becomes "asked", and present "do you know" changes to past "if he knew". "Excuse me" is expressed as "politely".

(b) Greetings like "Good morning" are kept in reported speech as “greeted”.

(c) A past event ("last year") becomes "the previous year", and "was" becomes "had been" to maintain backshift in tense.

(d) "Will" becomes "would" in reported speech as the reporting verb is past.

(e) Exclamatory sentence — "Yay!" becomes "exclaimed with joy", and present perfect "scored" becomes past perfect "had scored".

Question #98 (ID: 485921)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) He said, “Hello! I am feeling great today.”

(b) The boy said, “Can I borrow your eraser?”

(c) The girl says, “I am reading about the events of the July Revolution.”

(d) The girl said, “I love eating pithas during Pohela Boishakh.”

(e) He said to me, “Please pass the salt.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) He said hello and added that he was feeling great that day.

(b) The boy asked if he could borrow my eraser.

(c) The girl says that she is reading about the events of the July Revolution.

(d) The girl said that she loved eating pithas during Pohela Boishakh.

(e) He requested me to pass the salt.

Explanation:
(a) Greeting "Hello!" is reported as such, and present continuous "am feeling" becomes past continuous "was feeling"; "today" becomes "that day".

(b) Question with modal → "asked if he could"; "Can I" becomes "if he could".

(c) "Says" is present tense, so no tense change: "I am reading" becomes "she is reading".

(d) Simple present tense becomes simple past; "I love" → "she loved".

(e) "Please" indicates a request, so "said to" becomes "requested", and imperative becomes "to pass".

Question #99 (ID: 485922)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) The teacher said, "The earth is round."

(b) I said to her, "May you be happy in your life."

(c) The teacher said to the student, "Let us discuss gardening."

(d) Father said to his son, “Why did you not go to school yesterday?”

(e) She said, “Alas! I am undone.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The teacher said that the earth is round.

(b) I wished her that she might be happy in her life.

(c) The teacher proposed to the student that they should discuss gardening.

(d) Father asked his son why he had not gone to school the previous day.

(e) She exclaimed with sorrow that she was undone.

Explanation:
(a) This is a universal truth, so no tense change — remains "is".

(b) Optative sentence — "May you" becomes "wished that she might"; subject and object adjusted.

(c) "Let us" is a proposal, so we use "proposed that we should". "Said to" becomes "proposed to".

(d) Interrogative sentence in past tense; "Why did you not go" becomes "why he had not gone"; "yesterday" becomes "the previous day".

(e) Exclamatory sentence expressing grief — "Alas!" becomes "exclaimed with sorrow", and tense remains present for "am undone".

Question:
Change the narrative style of the following sentences.

(a) The girl said, “How beautiful the rainbow is!”

(b) The doctor said to the patient, “Don’t take tea for some days.”

(c) She said, “The boy may go.”

(d) He said to me, “Have you done your duty?”

(e) I said, “May her soul rest in peace.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The girl exclaimed with wonder that the rainbow was very beautiful.

(b) The doctor advised the patient not to take tea for some days.

(c) She said that the boy might go.

(d) He asked me if I had done my duty.

(e) I prayed that her soul might rest in peace.

Explanation:
(a) Exclamatory → becomes “exclaimed with wonder”; sentence converted to assertive form.

(b) Negative imperative → becomes “advised not to take”.

(c) Modal “may” changes to “might” in indirect speech.

(d) Interrogative → “Have you done” becomes “if I had done”.

(e) Optative prayer → "May" becomes "might", and "said" becomes "prayed".

Sub-Questions:

In this way, they can’t finish a work when they (g) — it. Then they say, “Alas! If we were not (h) — about our jobs when we had a lot of (i) — time, we could be (j) —.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) in (b) a (c) it (d) put (e) off (f) sure (g) start (h) careless (i) spare (j) successful

Explanation:
A stitch in time saves nine. This is a very well-known proverb. Some people don’t care for it. They put off a job off tomorrow, though they are not sure whether the day will come. In this way, they can’t finish a work when they start it. Then they say, “Alas! If we were not careless about our jobs when we had a lot of spare time, we could be successful.”

In this way, they can’t finish a work when they (g) — it. Then they say, “Alas! If we were not (h) — about our jobs when we had a lot of (i) — time, we could be (j) —.”

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) in (b) a (c) it (d) put (e) off (f) sure (g) start (h) careless (i) spare (j) successful

Explanation:
A stitch in time saves nine. This is a very well-known proverb. Some people don’t care for it. They put off a job off tomorrow, though they are not sure whether the day will come. In this way, they can’t finish a work when they start it. Then they say, “Alas! If we were not careless about our jobs when we had a lot of spare time, we could be successful.”

Question #214 (ID: 485803)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) We are proud of our freedom fighters. (Interrogative)

(b) Their contribution will always be remembered. (Active)

(c) The common people inspired them. (Interrogative)

(d) Today many of them do not lead a comfortable life. (Affirmative)

(e) I wish they would live a sound life. (Optative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Aren't we proud of our freedom fighters?

(b) People will always remember their contribution.

(c) Didn’t the common people inspire them?

(d) Today many of them lead an uncomfortable life.

(e) May they live a sound life.

Explanation:
(a) Interrogative করতে auxiliary verb “Aren’t” দিয়ে শুরু হয়।

(b) Passive কে Active করতে object কে subject করা হয়: "people"।

(c) Interrogative: “Didn’t” দিয়ে প্রশ্ন শুরু করা হয়।

(d) Negative থেকে affirmative করতে “do not lead” কে “lead” করা হয় এবং “comfortable” → “uncomfortable”।

(e) Optative রূপে “May” দিয়ে কামনার প্রকাশ করা হয়।

Question #215 (ID: 485804)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) A day labourer is known to everyone. (Make it active)

(b) He is not lazy and apathetic. (Make it affirmative)

(c) He is always dependent on his employer. (Make it negative)

(d) He is neglected in the society. (Make it interrogative)

(e) Let's be respectful to day labourers. (Make it assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Everyone knows a day labourer.

(b) He is active and attentive.

(c) He is not always independent of his employer.

(d) Is he not neglected in the society?

(e) We should be respectful to day labourers.

Explanation:
(a) Passive কে active করতে subject (Everyone) কে সামনে আনা হয়।

(b) Negative থেকে affirmative করতে “not lazy and apathetic” এর বিপরীত “active and attentive”।

(c) Negative রূপে “not independent” ব্যবহার করা হয়।

(d) Interrogative করতে “Is he not…” দিয়ে শুরু করতে হয়।

(e) “Let’s” এর assertive রূপ: “We should…”

Question #216 (ID: 485805)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Patriotism is not a trivial virtue. (Affirmative)

(b) Everyone should possess this noble quality. (Optative)

(c) An unpatriotic man is hated by all. (Active)

(d) Everybody hates an unpatriotic man. (Interrogative)

(e) He should respect his country. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Patriotism is a great virtue.

(b) May everyone possess this noble quality.

(c) All hate an unpatriotic man.

(d) Doesn't everybody hate an unpatriotic man?

(e) Respect your country.

Explanation:
(a) “Not a trivial” এর affirmative “a great virtue”।

(b) Optative বাক্য “May” দিয়ে শুরু হয়।

(c) Passive কে active করলে subject “All” এবং verb “hate” ব্যবহার হয়।

(d) Interrogative করার জন্য auxiliary “Doesn't” দিয়ে শুরু করতে হয়।

(e) Imperative এ subject বাদ দিয়ে মূল verb দিয়ে শুরু হয়।

Question #217 (ID: 485806)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Most of our people are illiterate. (Make it negative)

(b) It is so poor that we cannot imagine it. (Make it affirmative)

(c) It is the duty of the educated to teach the illiterate. (Make it interrogative)

(d) In this way, illiteracy can be removed from our society. (Make it active)

(e) Literate the illiterate. (Assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Most of our people are not literate.

(b) It is extremely poor.

(c) Isn't it the duty of the educated to teach the illiterate?

(d) In this way, we can remove illiteracy from our society.

(e) We should literate the illiterate.

Explanation:
(a) Negative রূপে “illiterate” এর বিপরীত “not literate” হয়।

(b) Affirmative করলে “so...that” বাদ দিয়ে “extremely” ব্যবহার হয়।

(c) Interrogative করতে “Isn't it…” দিয়ে শুরু করা হয়।

(d) Passive → Active: “we can remove” রূপে পরিবর্তন।

(e) Assertive করতে “We should…” যুক্ত করা হয়।

Question #218 (ID: 485807)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) As soon as we got the newspaper, we became happy. (Negative)

(b) Newspaper contains important news for us. (Passive)

(c) We are to practice the habit of reading newspaper. (Passive)

(d) Only reading newspaper gives us delight. (Negative)

(e) We should read a newspaper daily. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) No sooner had we got the newspaper than we became happy.

(b) Important news is contained in the newspaper for us.

(c) The habit of reading newspaper is to be practiced by us.

(d) Nothing but reading newspaper gives us delight.

(e) Read a newspaper daily.

Explanation:
(a) Negative রূপে “No sooner…than” ব্যবহার করা হয়।

(b) Passive: “is contained” ব্যবহৃত হয় “contains” এর পরিবর্তে।

(c) Passive voice: “is to be practiced” রূপে রূপান্তর হয়।

(d) “Only” negative রূপে “Nothing but…” দ্বারা রূপান্তর হয়।

(e) Imperative রূপে “should” বাদ দিয়ে মূল verb ব্যবহৃত হয়।

(c) Passive → Active: “Everyone trusts…”

(d) “Cannot but” Affirmative হলে “must” হয়।

(e) Assertive রূপে “We should…” ব্যবহার করা হয়।

(c) It stores honey in the hive. (Passive)

(d) It doesn't remain idle in spring. (Affirmative)

(e) We should protect bees. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:

(b) Does it not fly from flower to flower and take honey?

(d) It remains active in spring.

(e) Protect bees.

Explanation:

(b) Interrogative করতে auxiliary verb “Does” ব্যবহার করে প্রশ্নবোধক রূপ দেওয়া হয়।

(c) Passive: object “honey” কে subject করা হয় এবং “is stored” হয়।

(d) Affirmative: Negative “doesn’t remain idle” → “remains active”।

(e) Imperative: “should” বাদ দিয়ে মূল verb দিয়ে শুরু করা হয়।

Question #224 (ID: 485813)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Mr. Ant made proper use of his time. (Negative)

(b) Mr. Grasshopper used to pass his time in singing only. (Make it negative)

(c) He was a very worthless person. (Make it exclamatory)

(d) He could not but suffer at last. (Make it affirmative)

(e) We should learn a lesson from this story. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Mr. Ant did not waste his time.

(b) Mr. Grasshopper did not do anything but sing.

(c) What a worthless person he was!

(d) He had to suffer at last.

(e) Learn a lesson from this story.

Explanation:
(a) Negative: “made proper use” → “did not waste”।

(b) Negative রূপ: “did not do anything but sing”।

(c) Exclamatory: “What a worthless person…” কাঠামো ব্যবহার।

(d) Affirmative: “could not but” → “had to”।

(e) Imperative: “should” বাদ দিয়ে মূল verb দিয়ে শুরু।

Question #225 (ID: 485773)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) A flower is only a glowing gift of nature. (Negative)

(b) Who does not like flowers? (Affirmative)

(c) They are the symbol of love and beauty. (Interrogative)

(d) Flowers are used on different occasions. (Active)

(e) How significant the flower is to us! (Assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) A flower is not anything but a glowing gift of nature.

(b) Everyone likes flowers.

(c) Aren’t they the symbol of love and beauty?

(d) People use flowers on different occasions.

(e) The flower is very significant to us.

Explanation:
(a) Negative করার জন্য "only" → "not anything but" হয়।

(b) "Who does not like..." এর Affirmative হয় "Everyone likes..."

(c) Interrogative করতে auxiliary “Aren’t” দিয়ে শুরু করতে হয়।

(d) Passive থেকে Active করতে “People” কে subject হিসেবে আনা হয়।

(e) Assertive sentence: Exclamatory “How significant…” কে পরিবর্তন করে “very significant” ব্যবহার করা হয়।

Sub-Questions:

Question #226 (ID: 485774)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Honesty is a noble quality. (Interrogative)

(b) Isn't it greater than most other qualities in human life? (Affirmative)

(c) Everybody respects an honest man. (Passive)

(d) Mr. Ahmadullah was honest for which he was rewarded by his supervisor. (Active)

(e) You should be honest in our life. (Optative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Isn’t honesty a noble quality?

(b) It is greater than most other qualities in human life.

(c) An honest man is respected by everybody.

(d) His supervisor rewarded Mr. Ahmadullah for being honest in his works.

(e) May you be honest in our life.

Explanation:
(a) Interrogative করতে auxiliary “Isn’t” দিয়ে প্রশ্ন শুরু করা হয়।

(b) Affirmative করলে প্রশ্নবোধক রূপকে সরাসরি ইতিবাচক রূপে বলা হয়।

(c) Passive voice: object “an honest man” কে subject করা হয়।

(d) Active voice: agent (his supervisor) কে সামনে এনে verb “rewarded” ব্যবহৃত হয়।

(e) Optative: কামনা প্রকাশ করতে “May” দিয়ে শুরু করা হয়।

Question #227 (ID: 485775)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Bangladesh is a land of scenic beauty. (Interrogative)

(b) Cox’s Bazar sea beach is a wonderful tourist attraction. (Exclamatory)

(c) Everyone knows this. (Negative)

(d) This beach is visited by tourists from home and abroad. (Active)

(e) Our government is going to take many steps to make it more attractive. (Passive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Isn’t Bangladesh a land of scenic beauty?

(b) What a wonderful tourist attraction Cox’s Bazar sea beach is!

(c) There is no one who doesn’t know this.

(d) Tourists from home and abroad visit this beach.

(e) Many steps are going to be taken by our government to make it more attractive.

Explanation:
(a) Interrogative: “Isn’t” দিয়ে শুরু।

(b) Exclamatory: “What a...” গঠন ব্যবহার করা হয়।

(c) Negative: “Everyone knows” → “There is no one who doesn’t know”।

(d) Active: object “this beach” কে verb “visit” সহ subject করা হয়।

(e) Passive voice: “are going to be taken” কাঠামো ব্যবহার করে ভবিষ্যত কর্ম বোঝানো হয়।

Question #244 (ID: 485792)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Sir Jagadish Chandra Bose was not an ordinary man. (Affirmative)

(b) He made a great contribution to science. (Interrogative)

(c) He discovered the reaction of plants. (Negative)

(d) What a brilliant scientist he was! (Assertive)

(e) May students follow his path. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Sir Jagadish Chandra Bose was an extraordinary man.

(b) Did he not make a great contribution to science?

(c) He did not ignore the behavior of plants.

(d) He was a very brilliant scientist.

(e) Follow his path.

Explanation:
(a) “Not an ordinary man” → “extraordinary man” করে Affirmative অর্থ বজায় রাখা হয়েছে।

(b) Interrogative sentence গঠনের জন্য auxiliary verb “Did” বাক্যের শুরুতে বসানো হয়েছে।

(c) Negative রূপে অর্থ ঠিক রাখতে “did not ignore” ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে।

(d) Exclamatory → Assertive রূপে “What a” বাদ দিয়ে “very” দিয়ে adjective প্রকাশ।

(e) Optative → Imperative করতে “May” বাদ দিয়ে সরাসরি verb “Follow” দিয়ে শুরু।

Question #245 (ID: 485793)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Rabindranath Tagore was a poet and philosopher. (Negative)

(b) He never supported injustice. (Affirmative)

(c) He wrote many songs and poems. (Interrogative)

(d) What a great literary figure he was! (Assertive)

(e) May his works inspire us forever. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Rabindranath Tagore was not merely an artist.

(b) He always supported justice.

(c) Didn’t he write many songs and poems?

(d) He was a very great literary figure.

(e) Be inspired by his works forever.

Explanation:
(a) “Poet and philosopher” কে Negative করার জন্য “not merely an artist” বলা হয়েছে অর্থ না বদলে।

(b) “Never supported injustice” → “always supported justice” করে Affirmative।

(c) Interrogative গঠনে “Didn’t” দিয়ে প্রশ্ন তৈরি হয়েছে।

(d) “What a...” → “very + adjective” দিয়ে Assertive রূপ।

(e) “May” বাদ দিয়ে Imperative form-এ verb দিয়ে শুরু করা হয়েছে।

Question #246 (ID: 485794)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Dr. A.P.J. Abdul Kalam was not selfish. (Affirmative)

(b) He always encouraged students. (Negative)

(c) What an inspiring leader he was! (Assertive)

(d) He dreamed of a developed India. (Interrogative)

(e) May his dreams come true. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Dr. A.P.J. Abdul Kalam was selfless.

(b) He never discouraged students.

(c) He was a very inspiring leader.

(d) Didn’t he dream of a developed India?

(e) Work to fulfill his dreams.

Explanation:
(a) “Not selfish” → “selfless” দ্বারা Affirmative রূপে অর্থ বজায় থাকে।

(b) “Always encouraged” → “never discouraged” ব্যবহার করে Negative অথচ অর্থ ঠিক থাকে।

(c) “What an inspiring leader” → “very inspiring leader” করে Assertive sentence গঠন।

(d) Interrogative sentence গঠনে “Didn’t” ব্যবহার করে প্রশ্ন রূপ তৈরি করা হয়েছে।

(e) Optative → Imperative রূপে verb দিয়ে শুরু করে আদর্শ নির্দেশনা দেওয়া হয়েছে।

Question #247 (ID: 485795)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Daricomma helps students in many ways. (Negative)

(b) You can study from anywhere using Daricomma. (Interrogative)

(c) What a helpful platform Daricomma is! (Assertive)

(d) May every student benefit from Daricomma. (Imperative)

(e) Do not waste your time searching through multiple sites. (Affirmative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Daricomma does not fail to help students in many ways.

(b) Can’t you study from anywhere using Daricomma?

(c) Daricomma is a very helpful platform.

(d) Use Daricomma to benefit yourself.

(e) Save your time by using one unified platform.

Explanation:
(a) Negative sentence গঠনের জন্য “does not fail to help” রূপ ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে, যাতে মূল অর্থ বজায় থাকে।

(b) Interrogative করতে “Can’t you” দিয়ে প্রশ্নবোধক কাঠামো গঠন করা হয়েছে।

(c) Exclamatory → Assertive করতে “What a...” বাদ দিয়ে “very helpful platform” গঠন ব্যবহৃত হয়েছে।

(d) Optative → Imperative রূপে “May” বাদ দিয়ে “Use” দিয়ে নির্দেশমূলক বাক্য তৈরি হয়েছে।

(e) Negative Imperative “Do not waste” → Affirmative রূপে “Save your time” ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে অর্থ অপরিবর্তিত রেখে।

Question #248 (ID: 485796)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Daricomma is not a complicated platform. (Affirmative)

(b) Students never feel lost while using it. (Affirmative)

(c) Take unlimited practice tests. (Negative)

(d) Doesn’t Daricomma save students’ time? (Assertive)

(e) How smartly the topics are organized! (Assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Daricomma is a simple platform.

(b) Students always find it easy to use.

(c) Do not stop practicing regularly.

(d) Daricomma saves students’ time.

(e) The topics are very smartly organized.

Explanation:
(a) “Not complicated” → “simple” ব্যবহার করে Affirmative অর্থ বজায় রাখা হয়েছে।

(b) “Never feel lost” → “always find it easy” রূপে অর্থ অপরিবর্তিত রেখে Affirmative করা হয়েছে।

(c) Negative Imperative গঠনে “Do not” দ্বারা অন্য অর্থ বজায় রেখে পরিবর্তন।

(d) Interrogative → Assertive করতে auxiliary verb বাদ দিয়ে সরল বাক্য লেখা হয়েছে।

(e) Exclamatory → Assertive রূপে “How smartly” → “very smartly” ব্যবহৃত হয়েছে।

Question #249 (ID: 485797)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Daricomma is a one-stop solution for exam preparation. (Negative)

(b) Don’t ignore the importance of revision. (Affirmative)

(c) May every school adopt Daricomma. (Assertive)

(d) It brings all your resources in one place. (Interrogative)

(e) What a useful tool it is for students! (Assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Daricomma is not a scattered or confusing system.

(b) Always revise your topics before exams.

(c) We hope every school adopts Daricomma.

(d) Doesn’t it bring all your resources in one place?

(e) It is a very useful tool for students.

Explanation:
(a) “One-stop solution” কে Negative করতে “not a scattered or confusing system” ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে যাতে অর্থ বজায় থাকে।

(b) Negative Imperative → Affirmative করতে “Always revise” রূপ নেওয়া হয়েছে।

(c) Optative → Assertive করতে “May” বাদ দিয়ে “We hope” কাঠামো ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে।

(d) Assertive → Interrogative করতে auxiliary verb “Doesn’t” ব্যবহার করা হয়েছে।

(e) Exclamatory → Assertive করতে “What a” বাদ দিয়ে “very” adjective phrase ব্যবহৃত হয়েছে।

Question #250 (ID: 485798)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Hazi Mohammad Mohsin was a kind man. (Make it negative)

(b) He is a low paid employee. (Interrogative)

(c) He inherited vast property from his father and sister. (Make it passive)

(d) He did not marry. (Make it affirmative)

(e) During his lifetime he spent money lavishly. (Make it interrogative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Hazi Mohammad Mohsin was not an unkind man.

(b) Is he a low paid employee?

(c) Vast property was inherited by him from his father and sister.

(d) He married.

(e) Did he spend money lavishly during his lifetime?

Explanation:
(a) "Was a kind man" এর negative হলো "was not an unkind man" — এখানে 'kind' এর বিপরীত শব্দ 'unkind' ব্যবহৃত হয়েছে।

(b) "Is" auxiliary verb থাকায় Interrogative করতে সেটিকে বাক্যের শুরুতে আনা হয়।

(c) Active voice: "He inherited"; Passive এ করলে হয়: "Vast property was inherited by him..."।

(d) Negative "did not marry" কে affirmative করতে হলে simply "He married" লিখলেই হয়।

(e) Interrogative করতে হলে auxiliary verb "Did" বাক্যের শুরুতে এনে প্রশ্নবোধক রূপ দিতে হয়।

Question #251 (ID: 485799)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) We all should follow Mohammad Mohsin. (Imperative)

(b) Who does not know a postman? (Passive)

(c) He is a familiar figure. (Negative)

(d) He delivers letters, money orders, parcels, etc. to the addresses. (Passive)

(e) His responsibility is not insignificant. (Affirmative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Let us follow Mohammad Mohsin.

(b) A postman is known by everyone.

(c) He is not an unfamiliar figure.

(d) Letters, money orders, parcels, etc. are delivered to the addresses by him.

(e) His responsibility is significant.

Explanation:
(a) Imperative "should follow" কে 'Let us' দিয়ে নির্দেশমূলক করা হয়।

(b) "Who does not know..." কে passive এ করলে হয়: "A postman is known by everyone." — universal truth হিসেবে।

(c) Negative করতে familiar এর বিপরীত "unfamiliar" ব্যবহার করে "is not" দিয়ে বাক্য তৈরি হয়।

(d) Active থেকে Passive: Object গুলোকে subject করে "are delivered... by him" লেখা হয়।

(e) Double negative "not insignificant" কে affirmative করতে "significant" ব্যবহার করতে হয়।

Question #252 (ID: 485800)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) The causes of traffic jam are many. (Negative)

(b) The drivers don't obey traffic rules. (Affirmative)

(c) Overtaking tendency also causes traffic jam. (Interrogative)

(d) The govt. should construct spacious roads. (Passive)

(e) We all must work together to reduce traffic jams. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) The causes of traffic jam are not few.

(b) The drivers disobey traffic rules.

(c) Doesn't overtaking tendency also cause traffic jam?

(d) Spacious roads should be constructed by the govt.

(e) Let us all work together to reduce traffic jams.

Explanation:
(a) “Many” এর negative হয় “not few” অর্থাৎ বিপরীত ধারণা।

(b) “Don't obey” এর affirmative হয় “disobey” ব্যবহার করে।

(c) Interrogative করার জন্য auxiliary verb “doesn’t” দিয়ে শুরু করতে হয়।

(d) Passive voice: should + be + past participle = should be constructed.

(e) Imperative রূপে “Let us” দিয়ে শুরু করা হয় যা সম্মিলিত আহ্বান বোঝায়।

Question #253 (ID: 485801)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) English is a very important language. (Exclamatory)

(b) Isn't it an international language? (Assertive)

(c) We should learn it. (Passive)

(d) It is a necessary language. (Negative)

(e) You should learn the language to be competent. (Imperative)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) What an important language English is!

(b) It is an international language.

(c) It should be learnt by us.

(d) It is not an unnecessary language.

(e) Learn the language to be competent.

Explanation:
(a) Exclamatory sentence: What + adjective + noun + verb + subject.

(b) Assertive রূপে প্রশ্নটি সরাসরি বাক্য রূপে পরিবর্তন হয়।

(c) Passive: should + be + past participle (learnt)।

(d) Negative: “necessary” এর বিপরীত “unnecessary”, এবং not যোগ করা হয়।

(e) Imperative: subject (you) বাদ দিয়ে মূল verb দিয়ে শুরু হয়।

Question #254 (ID: 485802)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Change the following sentences as directed in the brackets.

(a) Pasteur was a famous scientist. (Interrogative)

(b) He found cures for several of them. (Negative)

(c) At first, he treated only animals. (Passive)

(d) He found a mad dog and injected some germs of the diseases into its blood. (Interrogative)

(e) May our medical science develop more and more. (Assertive)

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
(a) Wasn't Pasteur a famous scientist?

(b) He did not find cures for several of them.

(c) Only animals were treated by him at first.

(d) Did he not find a mad dog and inject some germs into its blood?

(e) It is hoped that our medical science will develop more and more.

Explanation:
(a) Interrogative: auxiliary verb + subject (Wasn't...)

(b) Negative রূপে "did not" ব্যবহার হয়।

(c) Passive voice: object “animals” কে subject করে রূপান্তর করা হয়।

(d) প্রশ্নবোধক বাক্য করতে হলে “Did he not” দিয়ে শুরু করা হয়।

(e) Optative বাক্য Assertive করতে হলে “It is hoped that…” দিয়ে শুরু হয়।

Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

william shakespeare the monarch of english literature was born on april 12 1564 in the stratford of avon his mother was mary arden and his father was john shakespeare he was not much educated he had little knowledge of grammar.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
William Shakespeare, the monarch of English literature, was born on April 12, 1564, in the Stratford of Avon. His mother was Mary Arden and his father was John Shakespeare. He was not much educated; he had little knowledge of grammar.

Explanation:
Explanation: Capitalize the first word of each sentence and all proper nouns—e.g., "William Shakespeare," "English," "April," and "Stratford-upon-Avon." Use commas to separate short phrases (for clarity between clauses like the place and the following clause) and periods to end sentences so the text reads clearly and correctly.

Question #256 (ID: 485725)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

help me out he called to the magician my dear boy the man replied you had better first give me the lamp and lighten your load it is not the lamp that weighs me down answered aladin but lend me a hand as soon as i reach the ground i will give it to you

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
"Help me out!" he called to the magician. "My dear boy," the man replied, "you had better first give me the lamp and lighten your load." "It is not the lamp that weighs me down," answered Aladin, "but lend me a hand. As soon as I reach the ground, I will give it to you."

Explanation:
The corrected version capitalizes the first word of each sentence and the proper name "Aladin," and it uses quotation marks to mark the magician's and Aladin's spoken words. Commas separate dialogue tags from the speech (for example, "he called to the magician," "the man replied,") and periods end sentences so the meaning and sentence boundaries become clear.

"Thank you," said the client. "I am leaving your chamber."

Question #259 (ID: 485728)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

are you brothers the mistress of the house said turning to the dervishes no by allah they said we are poor wanderers who met by mere chance we pray for allah's pardon

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
"Are you brothers?" the mistress of the house said, turning to the dervishes. "No, by Allah," they said, "we are poor wanderers who met by mere chance. We pray for Allah's pardon."

Explanation:
Capitalization rules require starting each sentence and proper nouns like "Allah" with a capital letter, and punctuation must mark quoted speech and sentence boundaries (question mark for a question, commas to set off tags, apostrophe for possession). So the passage is corrected by placing quotation marks around the spoken lines, using a question mark after "Are you brothers?", commas to offset the speaker tags, and an apostrophe in "Allah's" to show possession.

Question #263 (ID: 485732)
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

mr. Anik Akash a doctor has come to join the Upazila Health Complex. After joining he has started working. Suddenly a patient has come. The patient says, I’ve a pain in my stomach.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Mr. Anik Akash, a doctor, has come to join the Upazila Health Complex. After joining, he has started working. Suddenly, a patient has come. The patient says, "I've a pain in my stomach."

Explanation:
ব্যাখ্যা: শিরোনাম ও ব্যক্তির নাম, প্রতিষ্ঠান—যেমন "Mr.", "Anik Akash", "Upazila Health Complex"—প্রচলিতভাবে বড় হাতের অক্ষরে লেখা হয়; বাক্য শুরুেও বড় হাতের অক্ষর লাগে। "a doctor" এখানে নামের পর প্রকাশিত আপোোসিটিভ, তাই সেটার আগে ও পরে কমা লাগে, এবং "After joining,"–এর পরে ইনট্রোডাকটরি ফ্রেজ হিসেবে কমা দরকার। সরাসরি বলা কথার আগে কমা ও উদ্ধৃতি চিহ্ন ব্যবহার করতে হয়, আর কথাটা সঠিক ইংরেজিতে হওয়া উচিত: "I have a pain in my stomach" বা "I've got a pain in my stomach" ("I've a pain" সাধারণত গ্রহণযোগ্য নয়)।

Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

teaching is such a profession that helps to build a nation a teacher is both a guide and a pioneer he has to dedicate to this noble profession in order to guide the nation so he is called an architect of a new society if he neglects his duties social discipline will break down

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
Teaching is such a profession that helps to build a nation. A teacher is both a guide and a pioneer. He has to dedicate to this noble profession in order to guide the nation, so he is called an architect of a new society. If he neglects his duties, social discipline will break down.

Explanation:
Teaching is a profession that helps to build a nation. A teacher is both a guide and a pioneer. He must dedicate himself to this noble profession in order to guide the nation, and so he is called an architect of a new society. If he neglects his duties, social discipline will break down.

Explanation: The corrections use capitalization at the start of each sentence and appropriate punctuation (periods and a comma) to separate complete ideas and clauses. A reflexive pronoun ("himself") and the conjunction "and" were added for grammatical clarity. Proper punctuation and capitalization make the meaning clear and the sentence structure correct.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Type: CQ | Book: English 2nd Paper | Years:  | Boards:  | Tags: Important
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

oh my lord please do not kill the child said the woman let her have him the king said now everything is clear to me pointing to the woman he said to the servant give her the child she is the mother of the baby

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
"Oh my lord, please do not kill the child," said the woman.

"Let her have him," the king said. "Now everything is clear to me."

Pointing to the woman, he said to the servant, "Give her the child. She is the mother of the baby."

Explanation:
"Oh, my Lord, please do not kill the child," said the woman. "Let her have him," the king said. "Now everything is clear to me." Pointing to the woman, he added to the servant, "Give her the child; she is the mother of the baby."

This is correct because sentences begin with capital letters and direct speech is enclosed in quotation marks with commas or periods before speech tags; punctuation (commas, periods, semicolons) separates clauses and clarifies who is speaking.

how is your father bilkis said mr rahman he is very well thank you bilkis replid i am glad to hear that he is in good health said mr rahman.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
"How is your father, Bilkis?" said Mr. Rahman. "He is very well, thank you," Bilkis replied. "I am glad to hear that he is in good health," said Mr. Rahman.

Explanation:
Capitalize the first word of each sentence and all proper nouns (e.g., "Mr. Rahman", "Bilkis"), and use quotation marks for direct speech with the appropriate internal punctuation (a question mark for "How is your father?" and commas before dialogue tags). Also capitalize "I", place commas to separate dialogue tags (e.g., "…thank you," Bilkis replied), and end sentences with the correct terminal punctuation.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Question:
Rewrite the following passage using capitalization and punctuation.

the scientist shouted that he had done it addressing the scientist as sir the assistant congratulated him on what he had done the scientist replied that he had done something new.

Options:


Correct Answer: 

Solution:
The scientist shouted that he had done it. Addressing the scientist as "Sir," the assistant congratulated him on what he had done. The scientist replied that he had done something new.

Explanation:
The scientist shouted that he had done it, addressing the scientist as "Sir." The assistant congratulated him on what he had done. The scientist replied that he had done something new.

Explanation: Sentences begin with capital letters and end with full stops to show separate ideas; commas set off the phrase showing whom the speaker was addressing, and quotation marks indicate the form of address "Sir." This punctuation and capitalization make the meaning clear and the sentences grammatically correct.
